Jamison Brereton

51 (285)
Indra
Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra G─Бthina
12 verses: jagat─л 1тАУ3, triс╣гс╣нubh 4тАУ9, g─Бyatr─л 10тАУ12, arranged in trcas ╠е
The hymn falls into four sets of tr╠еcas, in three different meters. Since the hymn follows one of five verses, each tr╠еca should originally have been a single hymn, to conform to the normal patterns of arrangement within maс╣Зс╕Нalas. However, even if it did consist originally of four separate hymns, the evidence of larger ring composition discussed with regard to III.50 makes it likely that III.51 was an addition to the original Indra collection, which would once have ended with III.50.
The first two tr╠еcas consist of standard tropes of praise for Indra, with an empha sis on the songs and singers that express this praise. There are no strong indications of unity within the tr╠еcas. The third tr╠еca is devoted to IndraтАЩs drinking of soma in company with the Maruts and is thus appropriate to the Midday Pressing, like several other Indra hymns in this maс╣Зс╕Нala (III.32, 35, 47, 50). The final tr╠еca is even more insistently focused on IndraтАЩs soma-drinking.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra _________ 01-02 These two vss. have the same structure: p─Бdas acd are just accusatives qualifying the acc. ├нndram in b, and the b p─Бdas are essentially the same, with nom. pl.

g├нraс╕е + a verb that governs the accusatives. Though vs. 3 breaks the syntax, Indra still appears first by name in p─Бda b.

рдЕрдм рдмрд╛рд░рд╣ рдЛрдЪрд╛рд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЗрдХреНрдХрд╛рдирд╡реЗрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХрд╛ рдЖрд░рдореНрдн рд╣реИред рдЙрд╕рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рдердо рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛ ! рдмрд╣реБрдд рдЬрдиреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рд╕рддреНрдХреГрдд рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдУрдВ рдХреЗ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдореЗрдВ рд╕рдорд░реНрде рдЬрд┐рд╕ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдХреА рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд▓реЛрдЧ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░реЗрдВ, рдЙрд╕реА рдХреЗ рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧ рд╢рд░рдг рдЬрд╛рдУ реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдмреГрд╣рддреАрд░реНрдЧрд┐рд░реЛ рджрд┐рд╡реЗрджрд┐рд╡реЗ рд╕реБрд╡реГрдХреНрддрд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрдпрдВ рдЪрд░реНрд╖рдгреАрдзреГрддрдВ рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдореБрдХреНрдереНрдпрдВ рд╡рд╛рд╡реГрдзрд╛рдирдВ рдкреБрд░реБрд╣реВрддрдордорд░реНрддреНрдпрдВ рдЬрд░рдорд╛рдгрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдорднреНрдпрдиреВрд╖рдд рддрдВ рдпреВрдпрдорд╛рд╢реНрд░рдпрдд реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рд░рд╛рдЬрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЪрд░реНрд╖рдгреАрдзреГрддрдореН) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдзрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рд░рдореН (рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдореН) рдмрд╣реБрдзрдирдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН (рдЙрдХреНрдереНрдпрдореН) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреАрдпрдореН (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдореН) рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдирдореН (рдЧрд┐рд░рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдГ (рдмреГрд╣рддреАрдГ) рдмреГрд╣рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрд╛рдГ (рдЕрднрд┐, рдЕрдиреВрд╖рдд) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕реЗрдпреБрдГ (рд╡рд╛рд╡реГрдзрд╛рдирдореН) рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрдорд╛рдирдореН (рдкреБрд░реБрд╣реВрддрдореН) рдмрд╣реБрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рддреНрдХреГрддрдореН (рд╕реБрд╡реГрдХреНрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рд╕рдВрд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧреИрдГ (рдЕрдорд░реНрддреНрдпрдореН) рдорд░рдгрдзрд░реНрдорд░рд╣рд┐рддрдореН (рдЬрд░рдорд╛рдгрдореН) рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреНрддрдореН (рджрд┐рд╡реЗрджрд┐рд╡реЗ) рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рджрд┐рдирдореН реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMy praises constantly propitiate Indra, the object of many rites, the sender of rain, attended by the Maruts, the leader (of all), the giver of food, the destroyer of cities, the swift (in combat), the prompt (dispenser) of waters, the distributor of riches, the subduer of foes, the conferrer of heaven.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The superior man with a hundred resolves, a flood of powersтАФmy songs approach Indra from all sidesтАФ
winning spoils, splitting strongholds, swift at crossing the waters,
attending to the ordinances, attending closely, finding the sun.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. take arс╣Зav├бm as an unmarked simile, serving as goal to the verb in b: тАЬmy songs go to Indra, as if to the sea [Geldner тАЬ(wie) zu dem Meere,тАЭ Renou тАЬ(tel) un oc├йan,тАЭ Witzel Got┼Н more accurately but less persuasively тАЬ(wie) zu wallender FlutтАЭ].

The word is therefore only indirectly associated with Indra: they are both goals but need have nothing else in common. But given the parallelism in structure of vss. 1 and 2, I am reluctant to break the pattern of accusatives characterizing Indra by introducing this syntactic disjunction, and further the simile only makes good sense if arс╣Зav├б- really is a sea or the like, not an undulating flood. I think instead that Indra is directly described as a flood, the flood itself being characterized as ┼Ы─Бk├нn- тАШpossessing powersтАЩ.

The water-crossing mentioned here may simply be a reference to IndraтАЩs general leadership in crossing rivers and gaining new territory, but it may more specifically point to the famous crossing of King Sud─Бs dramatized in III.33 and referred to again in III.53.9, even though the poet Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra, not Indra, is the major actor there. The crossing is mentioned again in 9a.

Griffith

To Indra from all sides go forth my songs of praise, the Lord of Hundred Powers, strong, Hero, like the sea,
Swift, winner of the booty, breaker-down of forts, faithful and ever-glorious, finder of the light.

Geldner

Zu dem Ratreichen, wie zu dem Meere, zu dem machtvollen Herren, zu Indra kommen allenthalben meine Lobreden zu dem Gewinner des Siegespreises, dem Burgenbrecher, der eilig die Gew├дsser ├╝berschreitet, der dem Gesetz folgt, dem Begleiter, dem Sonnenfinder.

Grassmann

Dem hundertkr├дft’gen, wildbewegten, starken Mann, dem Indra eilen allseits meine Lieder zu; Der emsig, schnell ist, Kraft verleiht und Burgen bricht, zum Sitze eilt, zu H├╝lfe kommt und Glanz verschafft.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, the enfeebler (of adversaries), is praised as a mine of wealth; he is propitiated by righteous commendations; he is gratified in the dwelling of the offerer of oblations; glorify Indra, the conqueror, the destroyer of his enemies.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As a mine of wealth: ─Бkare vasoс╕е = he is praised to procure his aid in battle, which when successful, is the source of wealth or booty; ─Бk─лryate yuddh─Бrtham dhanam atra ity─Бkaro yuddhak, he is celebrated for the sake of war, for therein is wealth, therefore, ─Бkara is the same as yuddha; or, vasoс╕е jarayit─Б = weakener of the foe, vasu here meaning enemy

Jamison Brereton

The singer seeks admiration from him who distributes goods: Indra gives a friendly reception to his faultless rhythms,
for at the seat of Vivasvant [=ritual ground] he finds pleasure. Praise him, victorious in every way, the smasher of hostility.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although panasyate might make more sense if tr. тАЬexpresses admiration,тАЭ the other occurrences of this denom. stem and the related adj. panasy├║- all mean тАШattract/invite admirationтАЩ. Here the poet is hoping for a good reception from the recipient of his hymns, which he indeed receives in p─Бdas b and c. I have tr. the loc. phrase ─Бkar├й v├бsoс╕е as if ablative, to make the sense clearer. It could have been rendered тАЬтАж seeks admiration at (the hands of) him тАжтАЭ

Griffith

Where battle’s spoil is piled the singer winneth praise, for Indra taketh care of matchless worshippers.
He in Vivasvan’s dwelling findeth his delight: praise thou the ever-conquering slayer of the foe.

Geldner

Bei dem Spender des Gutes steht der S├дnger in Ehren. Indra bevorzugt die fehlerlosen Ges├дnge, denn am Sitze des Vivasvat wird er freundlich gestimmt. Preise den vollst├дndigen Sieger, der die Nachsteller erschl├дgt!

Grassmann

Beim Gutvertheiler ist der S├дnger gern gesehn, die fehlerlosen Lieder sind dem Indra lieb; Denn in dem Sitze des Vivasvat weilt er gern, den steten Sieger preise, der den Feind erschl├дgt.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThe priests glorify you, heroic leader of men, with praises and with prayers; Indra, the author of many delusions, exerts himself for (the acquisition of) strength; he from of old is the lord of this (oblation).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You [=Indra], the most manly of menтАФyou [=singers], recite to the hero forcefully with songs, with hymns.
Possessing many magical powers, he compacts himself together for
might. Reverence is his. From olden days he alone is lord.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Though this vs. begins a new tс╣Ыca in a different meter, it partially restores the syntactic structure of vss. 1-2: the first p─Бda presents Indra in the acc., the second one directs praises to him. Note also that nс╣Ыс╣З─Б╠Бm тАж nс╣Ы╠Бtamam picks up n├бram of 2a.

The structure is somewhat complicated by the fact that both (unnamed) Indra in p─Бda a and the (unnamed) subjects of the impv. arcat─Б in b are addressed in the 2nd ps.

This leads both Geldner and Renou to separate the two p─Бdas: Geldner pronounces p─Бda a an anacoluthon or ellipsis, while Renou supplies тАЬ(je te chante).тАЭ This fastidiouness seems unnecessary to me: the two referents of the 2nd persons are in different grammatical numbers and unlikely to be confused with each other for other reasons, and in a ritual situation both should be present (тАЬat the seat of Vivasvant,тАЭ 3c) and could both be directly addressed. The two instrumentals in p─Бda a (g─лrbh├нr uktha├нс╕е) also go better with the verb in b; cf., e.g., VI.22.1 ├нndraс╣Г t├бс╣Г g─лrbh├нr abhy ├аrca ─Бbh├нс╕е.

P─Бda d consists of two clauses, the nominal n├бmo asya and the short verb├иd clause prad├нva ├йka ─л┼Ыe, and so, contra GrassmannтАЩs suggestion (s.v. ─л┼Ы, col. 236, #8), the verb doesnтАЩt take an acc. here. For supposed exx. of тИЪ─л┼Ы with the acc., see comm. ad VII.32.18.

Full of all wondrous power he goes to conquest: worship is his, sole Lord from days aforetime.

рдорд░реНрддреНрдпреЗрд╖реБ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЗрд╖реБ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдирд┐рд╖реНрд╖рд┐рдзрдГ рдЕрдиреБрд╢рд╛рд╕рдирд╛рдирд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реАрдГ рд╣рд┐рддреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рднреВрддрд╛рдирд┐ рдирд╛рдирд╛рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╢рд╛рд╕рд┐рддреГрддреНрд╡реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдГ-тАЩ рдЙрдХреНрдердорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдп рд╢рдВрд╕реНрдпрдВ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдирдВ рдкреБрд░реБрдирд┐рд╖реНрд╖рд┐рдзреЗ ’ ( рдЛ. рд╕рдВ. рез. резреж. рел) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рд╢рд╛рд╕рдХрд╛рдп рддрд╕реНрдореИ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдп рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдкреБрд░реБ рдкреБрд░реВрдгрд┐ рдмрд╣реВрдирд┐ рд╡рд╕реВрдирд┐ рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдмрд┐рднрд░реНрддрд┐ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░реНрдзрд╛рд░рдпрддрд┐ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рдГ рджреНрдпреБрд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдГ рдУрд╖рдзреАрдГ рдУрд╖рдзрдпрдГ рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдЖрдкрдГ рдЬрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ рдЬреАрд░рдпрдГ ред рдЬреАрд░реНрдпрдиреНрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рдЬреАрд░рдпреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ ред рд╡рдирд╛рдирд┐ рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖рд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рдПрддреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЬреНрдЮрдпрд╛ рддрджреБрдкрднреЛрдЧрдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрдВ рд░рдпрд┐рдВ рдзрдирдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддрд┐ рее рдирд┐рд╖реНрд╖рд┐рдзрдГ ред тАШ рд╖рд┐рдзреБ рдЧрддреНрдпрд╛рдореН ’ ред рдХреНрд╡рд┐рдкреН ред рд╕рдВрд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдирд┐рд╕рдГ рд╕рдХрд╛рд░реЗрдг рдЗрдгреЛ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рдзрд╛рдирдВ рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдЕрдирд╛рджреГрддреНрдп рез рдЙрдкрд╕рд░реНрдЧрд╛рддреНрд╕реБрдиреЛрддрд┐┬░ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рд╖рддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдирд┐рд╕рдГ рд╕рдХрд╛рд░рд╕реНрдп тАШ рд╖реНрдЯреБрдирд╛ рд╖реНрдЯреБрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╖рддреНрд╡рдореН рее рее резрел рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMany are his prohibitions (against evil enjoined) to men; many are the treasures that the earth enshrines; for Indra the heavens, the plural nts, the waters, men and priests, preserve their riches.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Many are his prohibitions: purv─лr asya niс╣гidho martyeс╣гu = n─Бn─Б prak─Бr─Бс╣Зi anu┼Ы─Бsan─Бni, various kinds of commands or regulations; in RV. 1.95, pur┼лс╣Зis. idha = repeller of many foes; in both cases the substantive is from с╣гidh, to succeed, to go, with the proposition nir, out, ex, to exclude to prohibit

Jamison Brereton

Many are the tributes to him among mortals; many goods does the earth bear (for him).
For Indra the heavens, the plants, and the waters guard their wealth, and the lively (streams) and woods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The stem niс╣гс╣г├нdh- and related forms are difficult (see, inter alia, Scarlatta 596- 97). As Scarlatta points out, there is no obvious direct way to connect it with either тИЪs─Бdh тАШsucceedтАЩ or тИЪsidh тАШrepelтАЩ, and neither of these roots appears with n├нс╕е in the RV (though the latter does in post-RVic texts, but without relevant meaning; see Got┼Н, 1st Kl., 328). On the other hand, the semantic range of the word itself in context is relatively clear. It usually refers to something offered by inferiors to superiors.

GeldnerтАЩs Tribut (see his brief disc. in n. 5b) works pretty well. If we want to connect it to the root тИЪs─Бdh тАШsucceed, realize, reach the goalтАЩ, it may be seen as the material representation of the fulfillment (this is the тИЪs─Бdh part) of an obligation, and the n├нс╕е тАШforthтАЩ may reflect the proffering of these material goods.

I supply тАШstreamsтАЩ with j─лr├бyaс╕е on the basis of the other occurrence of this pl.

in II.17.3 pr├б j─лr├бyaс╕е sisrate тАж as well as the well-attested j─лr├б-d─Бnu- тАШpossessing lively dropsтАЩ. There is general agreement in the standard tr. that j─лr├н- refers to flowing water.

Griffith

Abundant are the gifts he gives to mortals: for him the earth bears a rich store of treasures.
The heavens, the growing plants, the living waters, the forest trees preserve their wealth for Indra.

Geldner

Reichlichen Tribut schuldet man ihm bei den Sterblichen; viele G├╝ter tr├дgt die Erde f├╝r ihn. F├╝r Indra bewahren die Himmel, die Pflanzen und die Gew├дsser, die Fl├╝sse, die W├дlder, ihren Reichtum.

Grassmann

Der Gaben viele hat er f├╝r die Menschen, und viele G├╝ter tr├дgt die weite Erde; Dem Indra hegen Himmel, Kr├дuter, Wasser, die raschen Str├╢me und die W├дlder Reichthum.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo you, Indra, (the pious) address prayers, and praises, and sacrifices; accept them, lord of horses; give all things, partake of this present oblation, and grant food to the worshippers.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For you the sacred formulations, for you the songs altogether have been established, o Indra of the fallow bays. Enjoy them!
Become a friend of help right now; o comrade, o good one, establish vigor for the singers.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the chiasmic structure t├║bhyam br├бhm─Бс╣Зi g├нraс╕е тАж t├║bhyam.

Geldner persuasively identifies ├бvaso n┼л╠Бtanasya as a genitive of quality.

Griffith

To thee, O Indra, Lord of Bays, for ever are offered prayers and songs: accept them gladly.
As Kinsman think thou of some fresh assistance; good Friend, give strength and life to those who praise thee.

Geldner

F├╝r dich sind die erbaulichen Reden, f├╝r dich, Indra, die Lobesworte allesamt bestimmt, o Falbenherr. Freue dich daran! Sei du der gute Freund neuester Hilfe! Guter Freund verleih den S├дngern Kraft!

Grassmann

Dir wurden Bitten, dir, o Indra, Lieder vereint gebracht, nimm an sie, Herr der F├╝chse; Auf neue H├╝lfe denke als Verwandter; o holder Freund, verleih den S├дngern Labung.

Elizarenkova

рднрдЯреНрдЯрднрд╛рд╕реНрдХрд░-рдЯреАрдХрд╛

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, accompanied, by the Maruts, drink the Soma at this ceremony as you have drunk of this libation of the son of ┼Ъ─Бry─Бti; your far-reaching and devout worshippers, being in security, adore you through their offerings.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

┼Ъ─Бrv─Бti: RV. 1.051.12; Yasus. 7.35; being in security: tava ┼Ыarman a viv─Бsanti, they worship you in the security, or unassailable plural ce, dependent on, or protected by you, tavasambandhini ┼Ыarmani nirb─Бdhasth─Бne stith─Бс╕е;

┼Ъarman = sukha-nimitte, for the sake of happiness; or, yaj├▒a-gс╣Ыha, the chamber of sacrifice

Jamison Brereton

O Indra along with the Maruts, drink the soma here, as you drank of the pressed (soma) beside ┼Ъ─Бry─Бta.
With your guidance, in your shelter, o champion, the wise poets of
good sacrifices seek their win.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. contains yet another implicit contrast between the aor. and pres. of тИЪp─Б тАШdrinkтАЩ: p─Бhi тАж y├бth─Б тАж ├бpibaс╕е. See comm. ad III.35.10, 36.3, 40.1-2, and 47.3.

It is not clear whether a contrast is also meant between the acc. s├│mam with p─Бhi (also 8a) and the (potentially partitive) genitive sut├бsya with ├бpibaс╕е and, if so, whether it is signaling some sort of aspectual distinction.

The verb ─Б╠Бviv─Бsanti lacks an object here, though it usually is construed with one. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) interpret it as тАШinviteтАЩ (presumably supplying тАШyouтАЩ), while Renou supplies the gods as object. I think the object slot has been intentionally left blank: with IndraтАЩs guidance and in his shelter they hope to win whatever they fancy, hence my somewhat awk. tr. тАЬseek their win.тАЭ Oberlies (Rel.RV I.403) suggests that this is a poetic contest, but I donтАЩt see any evidence of this beyond the plural.

Given the usual rendering of kav├н- elsewhere in the published translation, I would change the tr. here to тАШsage poetsтАЩ or just тАШpoetsтАЩ.

Griffith

Here, Indra, drink thou Soma with the Maruts, as thou didst drink the juice beside Saryata.
Under thy guidance, in thy keeping, Hero, the singers serve, skilled in fair sacrifices.

Indra, Marutbegleiteter, trink hier den Soma, wie du bei Saryata vom Safte trankst! Unter deiner F├╝hrung, in deinem Schutze, du Held, laden die Weisen mit sch├╢nem Opfer ein.

Grassmann

Hier trinke Soma mit den Maruts, Indra, wie bei ├Зarjata du den Saft getrunken; In deiner Huld, o Held, in deinem Schutze erfreuen sich die opferreichen Weisen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDo you, Indra, who is gratified by the Soma, drink the Soma that has been effused by us, together with your friends, the Maruts, at this ceremony; you who is invoked of many, and whom all the gods equipped as soon as born for the great battle (with the asuras).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Eagerly desirous, here drink the soma pressed by us, o Indra, with the Maruts as your comradesтАФ
as when all the gods busied themselves around you, just born, for great plunder, o much-invoked one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The connection between the two hemistichs in this vs. is not clear. The first unambiguously presents the here-and-now of the sacrifice, with an impv. and the adv.

ih├б тАШhereтАЩ, while the second harks back to IndraтАЩs primordial birth and the godsтАЩ attendance on it, expressed by an augmented imperf. (├бbh┼лс╣гan). There is no way to reconcile the temporal disjunction directly, so I have adopted GeldnerтАЩs makeshift: supplying тАЬ(wie damals),тАЭ though there is no overt representation of my тАЬasтАЭ (or his тАЬwie damalsтАЭ). There does not seem to be much semantic connection between the two halves either, unless we, the pressers and offerers, are being identified with the gods who served Indra at his birth.

Griffith

So eagerly desirous drink the Soma, our juice, O Indra, with thy friends the Maruts,
Since at thy birth all Deities adorned thee for the great fight, O thou invoked of many.

Geldner

Trink hier voll Verlangen den Soma, den von uns ausgepre├Яten mit den Marut, deinen Freunden, o Indra, wie damals als dich, den eben geborenen, alle G├╢tter zum gro├Яen Kampfe umringten, du Vielgerufener.

Grassmann

So trink, o Indra, lustig hier den Soma, hier unsern Trank vereinigt mit den Maruts; Als du geboren, schm├╝ckten alle G├╢tter zum grossen Kampf dich aus, o vielgerufner.

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, this is your friend for sending of the waters; they (the Maruts), the givers of strength, have yielded Indra gratification; may the devourer of Vс╣Ыtra drink with them the libation offered by the worshipper in his abode.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

At the crossing of the waters, o Maruts, he is a friend. They, who give favors, have applauded Indra.
Together with them let the Vr╠еtra-gnawer drink the pressed soma in the very seat of the pious worshiper.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The abrupt temporal shifts continue in this vs., exacerbated by shifts in person. The poet first addresses the Maruts in the 2nd ps. and asserts something about Indra in the present time (or so I [and the other standard tr.] take the nominal sentence without overt copula). In p─Бda b the Maruts are then referred to in the 3rd ps.

– though they are not named in this p─Бda, the other two occurrences of d─Б╠Бti-vararefer to them, and ├бnu тИЪmad is a signature verb of theirs – and in the past, in the augmented impf. ├бmandan. (Though the Saс╣Гhit─Б text transmits тАШmandan, the augment is metrically guaranteed.) This p─Бda seems an aside, reminding the audience of the MarutsтАЩ previous involvement with Indra. The vs. then shifts to the present time again, with the Maruts remaining in the 3rd ps., as potential drinking companions for Indra.

In 6c Indra was urged to become тАЬa friend of present helpтАЭ; what that present help was/should be is spelled out here, a friend тАЬat the water-crossing.тАЭ For watercrossing see comm. ad vs. 2 above. It is presumably not directly related to the MarutsтАЩ applause in p─Бda b, for they provide material and moral support at the Vс╣Ыtrasmashing, not in crossing waters.

III.51.9-10. Note that pibatu takes an acc. in 9cd, but a gen. in 10c, as with ├бpibaс╕е in 7b.

Griffith

He was your comrade in your zeal, O Maruts: they, rich in noble gifts, rejoiced in Indra.
With them together let the Vrtra-slayer drink in his home the worshipper’s libation.

Bei der ├Ьberschreitung der Gew├дsser ist dieser der gute Freund, o Marut. Es jubelten dem Indra die Wunschgew├дhrer zu. Mit ihnen zusammen soll der Vritravertilger den gepre├Яten Soma an des Opferspenders eigenem Sitze trinken.

Grassmann

Im schnellen Werk war er ein Freund euch, Maruts, dem Indra jauchzten zu die gabenreichen; Der Vritratilger trinke nun mit diesen im eignen Sitz des Frommen Somatr├дnke.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLord of riches, entitled to praise, this libation has been effused agreeably to (our) strength; do you drink of it quickly.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Because this pressed (drink) is right here at hand with its strength, o lord of benefits,
drink of it, o you who long for song.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first two p─Бdas of this vs. are variously translated. The problems are 1) the referent of id├бm and 2) the absence of a verb. My interpr. is closest to GeldnerтАЩs. If the referent of id├бm is the soma, we need only find a synonym for soma that is neuter; s├бvanam fits the bill and is elsewhere modified by sut├б-, as it can be here. As for the verb, I assume a form of тИЪas: the idiom ├бnu тИЪas means тАШbe at handтАЩ.

Griffith

So, Lord of affluent gifts, this juice hath been pressed for thee with strength
Drink of it, thou who lovest song.

Geldner

Diese Trankspende, die mit Kraft ausgepre├Яt ist, steht ja bereit, du Herr der Gaben. Trink doch davon, du Lobbegehrender!

Grassmann

Gebraut ist hier ringsum mit Kraft der Soma, o der Gaben Herr, So trink ihn denn, von Lied umt├╢nt.

Elizarenkova

Which(ever soma drink) will suit your nature, halt yourself at that pressing. Let it exhilarate you, who deserve the soma.

Incline thy body to this juice which suits thy Godlike nature well:
May it cheer thee who lovest it.

Zu ihm, der recht nach Wunsch dir sei, zum Safte lenke deinen Leib; Dich Somafreund berausche er.

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рд╕ рд╕реЛрдордГ рддреЗ рддрд╡ рдХреБрдХреНрд╖реНрдпреЛрдГ рдХреБрдХреНрд╖реЗрд░реБрднрдпреЛрдГ рдкрд╛рд░реНрд╢реНрд╡рдпреЛрдГ рдЙрднреМ рдкрд╛рд░реНрд╢реНрд╡реМ рдкреНрд░ рдЕрд╢реНрдиреЛрддреБ рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖реЗрдг рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддреБ ред рддрдерд╛ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгрд╛ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реЗрдг рд╕рд╣рд┐рддрдГ рд╕ рд╕реЛрдордГ рд╢рд┐рд░рдГ рд╢рд░реАрд░рдореН ред рдЕрд╡рдпрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛рд╡рдпрд╡реА рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрддреЗ ред рддреНрд╡рдЪреНрдЫрд░реАрд░рдВ рдкреНрд░ рдЕрд╢реНрдиреЛрддреБ ред рд╣реИ рд╢реВрд░ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рд░рд╛рдзрд╕реЗ рдзрдирд╛рдп рддрд╡ рдмрд╛рд╣реВ рдЕрдкрд┐ рдкреНрд░ рдЕрд╢реНрдиреЛрддреБ рее рдЕрд╢реНрдиреЛрддреБ ред рдЕрд╢реВ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддреМ ’ рдЗрд╕реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд▓реЛрдЯрд┐ рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рдкрд░рд╕реНрдореИрдкрджрдореН ред рдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрдГ ред рдХреБрдХреНрд╖реНрдпреЛрдГ ред тАШ рдЙрджрд╛рддреНрддрдпрдгреЛ рд╣рд▓реНрдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рддреН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддреЗрд░реБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН рее рее резрем рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay this libation, Indra, penetrate to your flanks; may it, (aided) by prayer, reach your head; may it spread, hero, through your arms, (that they may distribute) wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let it reach to your two cheeks, to your head, Indra, (accompanied) by a sacred formulationтАФ
to your two arms, o champion, for (you) to give.

Griffith

Brave Indra, let it work through both thy flanks, and through thy head by prayer,
And through thine arms, to prosper us.

Geldner

Er soll in deine Seiten dringen, in dein Haupt mit Erbauung, o Indra, in deine Arme zum Schenken, o Held!

Grassmann

Er dringe ein in deinen Bauch und durch Gebete in dein Haupt, Zum Schenken, Held, in deinen Arm.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдзрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдореН (VC)
  • рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░:
  • рдЧреЛрдкрд╡рди рдЖрддреНрд░реЗрдпрдГ рд╕рдкреНрддрд╡рдзреНрд░рд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╛
  • рд╡рд┐рд░рд╛рдбреНрдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░реА

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдУрдВ рдореЗрдВ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рдЬреЛ (рддреЗ) рдЖрдкрдХреЗ (рдХреБрдХреНрд╖реНрдпреЛрдГ) рдкреЗрдЯ рдХреЗ рдЖрд╕-рдкрд╛рд╕ рдХреЗ рднрд╛рдЧреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгрд╛) рдзрди рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд░рд╕ рдХреЛ (рдкреНрд░) (рдЕрд╢реНрдиреЛрддреБ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрд╡реИ рдФрд░ рд╣реЗ (рд╢реВрд░) рд╡реАрд░ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ ! (рддреЗ) рдЖрдкрдХреЗ (рд╢рд┐рд░рдГ) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рдЕрдЩреНрдЧ рдорд╕реНрддрдХ рдХреЛ (рдмрд╛рд╣реВ) рднреБрдЬрд╛рдУрдВ рдХреЛ (рд░рд╛рдзрд╕реЗ) рдзрди рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрд╡реЗ, рдЙрд╕рдХрд╛ рдЖрдк рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рд┐рдпреЗ реерезреирее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреН ! рд╡рд╣реА рд╡рд╕реНрддреБ рдЖрдкрдХреЛ рдЦрд╛рдирд╛ рддрдерд╛ рдкреАрдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рдХрд┐ рдЬреЛ рдкреЗрдЯ рдореЗрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛ рддрдерд╛ рд╡рд┐рдХреГрдд рд╣реЛ рд░реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рдХрд░рдХреЗ рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рдХрд╛ рди рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░реЗ рдФрд░ рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рдЖрдкрдореЗрдВ рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рдмрдврд╝ рдХрд░ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдп рдФрд░ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдп рдмрдврд╝реЗ реерезреирее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рдХреЗ рдзрд░реНрдорд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкрд┐рдЫрд▓реЗ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдЗрдХреНрдпрд╛рд╡рдирд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рд╕реЛрд▓рд╣рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ ! рдпрд╕реНрддреЗ рдХреБрдХреНрд╖реНрдпреЛрд░реНрдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгрд╛ рд╕рд╣ рд░рд╕рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╢реНрдиреЛрддреБред рд╣реЗ рд╢реВрд░ рддрд╡ рд╢рд┐рд░реЛ рдмрд╛рд╣реВ рд░рд╛рдзрд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╢реНрдиреЛрддреБ рддрдВ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдкрд╛рд▓рдп реерезреирее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдкреНрд░) (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рдЕрд╢реНрдиреЛрддреБ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддреБред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рдкрд░рд╕реНрдореИрдкрджрдореНред (рдХреБрдХреНрд╖реНрдпреЛрдГ) рдЙрджрд░рдкрд╛рд░реНрд╢реНрд╡рдпреЛрдГ (рдкреНрд░) (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд░рд╛рдЬрд╡рд░ (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгрд╛) рдзрдиреЗрди (рд╢рд┐рд░рдГ) рдЙрддреНрддрдорд╛рдЩреНрдЧрдореН (рдкреНрд░) (рдмрд╛рд╣реВ) рднреБрдЬреМ (рд╢реВрд░) (рд░рд╛рдзрд╕реЗ) рдзрдирд╛рдп реерезреирее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрдБрд╕реНрддрджреЗрд╡ рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛рд╜рд╜рд╢рд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рдкрд╛рддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рдЪ рдпрджреБрджрд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдп рд╡рд┐рдХреГрддрдВ рд╕рджреНрд░реЛрдЧрд╛рдиреБрддреНрдкрд╛рджреНрдп рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдВ рди рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕реНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпреЗрди рд╕рддрддрдВ рддреНрд╡рдпрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдВ рдЪ рд╡рд░реНрдзреЗрддреЗрддрд┐ реерезреирее ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдзрд░реНрдорд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрд╛рд╜рдзрд┐рдХрдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╖реЛрдбрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрде -рд╣реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛! рд░реЛрдЧ рд╣реЛрдКрди рдмреБрджреНрдзреАрдЪрд╛ рдирд╛рд╢ рд╣реЛрдгрд╛рд░ рдирд╛рд╣реА рдЕрд╕реЗ рдЦрд╛рди-рдкрд╛рди рддреВ рдХреЗрд▓реЗ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗ рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рдирд┐рд░рдВрддрд░ рдмреБрджреНрдзреА рд╡рд╛рдвреВрди рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рд╡рд╛рдвреЗрд▓. рее резреи рее
